title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.gd" title=".gd">.gd</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Plus trace of <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawak</a>&#160;/&#32;<a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Carib</a>.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Grenada</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Grenada.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c0/En-us-Grenada.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Grenada.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">grih-<span style="font-size:90%">NAY</span>-d\xc9\x99</i></a>) is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> in the southeastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> consisting of the island of Grenada and six smaller islands at the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a> island chain. It is located northwest of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, northeast of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and southwest of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. Its size is 348.5 square kilometres (134.6&#160;sq&#160;mi), and it had an estimated population of 107,317<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> in 2016. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George&#39;s, Grenada">St. George\'s</a>. Grenada is also known as the "Island of Spice" due to its production of <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a> crops, of which it is one of the world\'s largest exporters. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_birds" title="List of national birds">national bird</a> of Grenada is the <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Grenada_dove" title="Grenada dove">Grenada dove</a>.\n</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">arrival of Europeans in the Americas</a>, Grenada was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawaks</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted Grenada in 1498 during his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a> to the Americas. Although it was deemed the property of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King of Spain</a>, there are no records to suggest the Spanish ever landed or settled on the island. Following several unsuccessful attempts by Europeans to colonise the island due to resistance from the Island Caribs, <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> settlement and colonisation began in 1650 and continued for the next century. On 10 February 1763, Grenada was ceded to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>. British rule continued, except for a <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Grenada_1779" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Grenada 1779">period of French rule</a> between 1779 and 1783, until 1974. From 1958 to 1962, Grenada was part of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of the West Indies">Federation of the West Indies</a>, a short-lived federation of <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indian colonies</a>. On 3 March 1967, Grenada was granted full autonomy over its internal affairs as an <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">Associated State</a>. <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a> was the first Premier of the Associated State of Grenada from March to August 1967. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gairy" title="Eric Gairy">Eric Gairy</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Grenada#Premier_of_Associated_state_of_Grenada_(1967-1974)" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Grenada">Premier</a> from August 1967 until February 1974.\n</p><p>Independence was granted on 7 February 1974, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gairy" title="Eric Gairy">Eric Gairy</a>, who became the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Grenada" title="List of heads of government of Grenada">Prime Minister of Grenada</a>. In March 1979, the <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism\xe2\x80\x93Leninism">Marxist\xe2\x80\x93Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement" title="New Jewel Movement">New Jewel Movement</a> overthrew Gairy\'s government in a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat</a> and established the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Revolutionary Government">People\'s Revolutionary Government</a> (PRG), headed by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> as Prime Minister. On 19 October 1983, hard-line Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Coard" title="Bernard Coard">Bernard Coard</a> and his wife Phyllis, backed by the Grenadian Army, led a coup against the government of Maurice Bishop and placed Bishop under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a>. Bishop was later freed by popular demonstration and attempted to resume power, but he was captured and executed by soldiers. On 25 October 1983, forces from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Regional_Security_System" title="Regional Security System">Regional Security System</a> (RSS) invaded Grenada in a U.S.-led operation code-named <i><a href="/wiki/US_invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="US invasion of Grenada">Operation Urgent Fury</a></i>. The invasion was highly criticised by the governments of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>. Elections were held in December 1984 and were won by the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_National_Party" title="Grenada National Party">Grenada National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a>, who served as Prime Minister until his death in December 1989.\n</p><p>On 7 September 2004, after being hurricane-free for 49&#160;years, the island was directly hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a>, which damaged or destroyed 90% of the island\'s homes. On 14 July 2005, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Emily_(2005)" title="Hurricane Emily (2005)">Hurricane Emily</a> struck the northern part of the island causing an estimated <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">USD</a> $110&#160;million (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Caribbean Dollar">EC$</a>297&#160;million) worth of damage.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The origin of the name "Grenada" is obscure, but it is likely that <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> sailors renamed the island for the city of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> By the beginning of the 18th century, the name "Grenada", or "la Grenade" in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, was in common use.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a> to the region in 1498, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted Grenada and named it "La Concepci\xc3\xb3n" in honour of the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Virgin Mary</a>. It is said that he may have actually named it "Assumpci\xc3\xb3n", but it is uncertain, as he is said to have sighted what are now Grenada and Tobago from a distance and named them both at the same time. However, history has accepted that it was Tobago he named "Assumpci\xc3\xb3n" and Grenada he named "La Concepci\xc3\xb3n".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1499, the Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> travelled through the region with the Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">Alonso de Ojeda</a> and mapmaker <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cosa" title="Juan de la Cosa">Juan de la Cosa</a>. Vespucci is reported to have renamed the island "Mayo", which is how it appeared on maps for around the next 20 years.\n</p><p>In the 1520s, the Spanish named the islands to the north of Mayo as <i>Los Granadillos</i> (Little Granadas), presumably after the mainland Spanish town. Shortly after this, Mayo disappeared from Spanish maps and an island called "Granada" took its place. Although it was deemed the property of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King of Spain</a>, there are no records to suggest the Spanish ever landed or settled on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After French settlement and colonisation in 1650, the French named their colony "La Grenade". On 10 February 1763, the island of La Grenade was ceded to the British under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a>. The British renamed it "Grenada", one of many place name <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">anglicisations</a> they carried out on the island during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Grenada" title="History of Grenada">History of Grenada</a></div>\n<p>About 2 million years ago, Grenada was formed as an underwater volcano. Before the arrival of Europeans, Grenada was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawaks</a> and, subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted Grenada in 1498 during his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">third voyage</a> to the new world.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="French_colony_.281649.E2.80.931763.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colony_(1649\xe2\x80\x931763)">French colony (1649\xe2\x80\x931763)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: French colony (1649\xe2\x80\x931763)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1649 a French expedition of 203 men from <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> led by Jacques du Parquet founded a permanent settlement on Grenada. Within months this led to conflict with the local islanders which lasted until 1654 when the island was completely subjugated by the French.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The indigenous islanders who survived either left for neighbouring islands or retreated to remoter parts of Grenada where they were marginalised\xe2\x80\x94the last distinct communities disappeared during the 1700s.\n</p><p>Warfare continued during the 1600s between the French on Grenada and the Caribs of present-day <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. The French named their <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empires" class="mw-redirect" title="French colonial empires">new colony</a> La Grenade, and the economy was initially based on <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">indigo</a>. The French established a capital known as <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s, Grenada">Fort Royal</a> (later St. George). To shelter from hurricanes the French navy would often take refuge in the capital\'s natural harbour, as no nearby French islands had a natural harbour to compare with that of Fort Royal. The British captured Grenada during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a> in 1762.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="British_colony_.281763.E2.80.931974.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colony_(1763\xe2\x80\x931974)">British colony (1763\xe2\x80\x931974)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: British colony (1763\xe2\x80\x931974)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Grenada was formally ceded to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1763. The French <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Grenada_1779" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Grenada 1779">re-captured the island</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Comte_d%27Estaing" class="mw-redirect" title="Comte d&#39;Estaing">Comte d\'Estaing</a> won the bloody land and naval <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grenada" title="Battle of Grenada">Battle of Grenada</a> in July 1779. However the island was restored to Britain with the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Peace of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Versailles</a> in 1783. Britain was hard pressed to overcome a pro-French revolt in 1795\xe2\x80\x9396 led by <a href="/wiki/Julien_Fedon" class="mw-redirect" title="Julien Fedon">Julien Fedon</a>.\n</p><p>Nutmeg was introduced to Grenada in 1843 when a merchant ship called in on its way to England from the East Indies. The ship had a small quantity of nutmeg trees on board which they left in Grenada, and this was the beginning of Grenada\'s nutmeg industry that now supplies nearly 40% of the world\'s annual crop.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1877 Grenada was made a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a>. Theophilus A. Marryshow founded the Representative Government Association (RGA) in 1917 to agitate for a new and participative constitutional dispensation for the Grenadian people. Partly as a result of Marryshow\'s lobbying, the Wood Commission of 1921\xe2\x80\x9322 concluded that Grenada was ready for constitutional reform in the form of a modified Crown colony government. This modification granted Grenadians the right to elect five of the 15 members of the Legislative Council, on a restricted property franchise enabling the wealthiest 4% of adult Grenadians to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Toward_independence_.281950.E2.80.931974.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Toward_independence_(1950\xe2\x80\x931974)">Toward independence (1950\xe2\x80\x931974)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Toward independence (1950\xe2\x80\x931974)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1950 <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gairy" title="Eric Gairy">Eric Gairy</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_United_Labour_Party" title="Grenada United Labour Party">Grenada United Labour Party</a>, initially as a <a href="/wiki/Trades_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Trades union">trades union</a>, which led the 1951 <a href="/wiki/General_strike" title="General strike">general strike</a> for better working conditions. This sparked great unrest\xe2\x80\x94so many buildings were set ablaze that the disturbances became known as the "red sky" days\xe2\x80\x94and the British authorities had to call in military reinforcements to help regain control of the situation. On October 10, 1951, Grenada held its first general elections on the basis of universal adult suffrage,<sup id="cite_ref-bigdrumnation.org_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigdrumnation.org-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> with Gairy\'s party winning six of the eight seats contested.<sup id="cite_ref-bigdrumnation.org_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bigdrumnation.org-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> From 1958 to 1962 Grenada was part of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_the_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation of the West Indies">Federation of the West Indies</a>.\n</p><p>On March 3, 1967, Grenada was granted full autonomy over its internal affairs as an Associated State. <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a> was the first Premier of the Associated State of Grenada from March to August 1967. Eric Gairy served as <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Grenada#Premier_of_Associated_state_of_Grenada_(1967-1974)" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Grenada">Premier from August 1967</a> until February 1974.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Post-independence_coups_.281974.E2.80.931983.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_coups_(1974\xe2\x80\x931983)">Post-independence coups (1974\xe2\x80\x931983)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-independence coups (1974\xe2\x80\x931983)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101,_Berlin,_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada,_Bootsfahrt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101%2C_Berlin%2C_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada%2C_Bootsfahrt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="537" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1982-0610-101,_Berlin,_Besuch_Regierungsdelegation_Grenada,_Bootsfahrt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> visiting East Germany, 1982</div></div></div>\n<p>Independence was granted on February 7, 1974, under the leadership of Eric Gairy, who became the first Prime Minister of Grenada.\n</p><p>Civil conflict gradually broke out between Eric Gairy\'s government and some opposition parties including the Marxist <a href="/wiki/New_Jewel_Movement" title="New Jewel Movement">New Jewel Movement</a> (NJM). Gairy\'s party won elections in 1976. The opposition did not accept the result, accusing it of fraud.\n</p><p>In March 1979, the New Jewel Movement launched a <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a> which removed Gairy, suspended the constitution, and established a <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Revolutionary Government">People\'s Revolutionary Government</a> (PRG), headed by <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop" title="Maurice Bishop">Maurice Bishop</a> who declared himself prime minister. His <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism\xe2\x80\x93Leninism">Marxist\xe2\x80\x93Leninist</a> government established close ties with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, Nicaragua, and other <a href="/wiki/Communist_bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist bloc">communist bloc</a> countries. All political parties except for the New Jewel Movement were banned and no elections were held during the four years of PRG rule.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Invasion_by_the_United_States_.281983.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_by_the_United_States_(1983)">Invasion by the United States (1983)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Invasion by the United States (1983)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">Invasion of Grenada</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/220px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/330px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg/440px-Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3020" data-file-height="1950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Caribbean_Defense_Force.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the Eastern Caribbean Defence Force during the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coup_and_execution_of_Maurice_Bishop">Coup and execution of Maurice Bishop</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Coup and execution of Maurice Bishop">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Some years later a dispute developed between Bishop and certain high-ranking members of the NJM. Though Bishop cooperated with <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> on various trade and foreign policy issues, he sought to maintain a "non-aligned" status. Bishop had been taking his time making Grenada wholly <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a>, encouraging private-sector development in an attempt to make the island a popular tourist destination. Hardline <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> party members, including <a href="/wiki/Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist">communist</a> Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Coard" title="Bernard Coard">Bernard Coard</a>, deemed Bishop insufficiently revolutionary and demanded that he either step down or enter into a power-sharing arrangement.\n</p><p>On October 19, 1983, Bernard Coard and his wife Phyllis, backed by the Grenadian Army, led a coup against the government of Maurice Bishop and placed Bishop under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a>. These actions led to street demonstrations in various parts of the island. Bishop had enough support from the population that he was eventually freed after a demonstration in the capital. When Bishop attempted to resume power, he was captured and executed by soldiers along with seven others, including government cabinet ministers. The Coard regime then put the island under martial law.\n</p><p>After the execution of Bishop, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Revolutionary_Army_(Grenada)" title="People&#39;s Revolutionary Army (Grenada)">People\'s Revolutionary Army</a> (PRA) formed a military government with General <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Austin" title="Hudson Austin">Hudson Austin</a> as chairman. The army declared a four-day total curfew, during which anyone leaving their home without approval would be shot on sight.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_and_allied_response_and_reaction">United States and allied response and reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United States and allied response and reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/220px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/330px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg/440px-M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2920" data-file-height="1990" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M102_howitzers_during_Operation_Urgent_Fury.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M102 howitzers of <a href="/wiki/320th_Field_Artillery_Regiment" title="320th Field Artillery Regiment">320th Field Artillery Regiment</a> firing during the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The overthrow of a moderate government by one which was strongly pro-communist worried the administration of US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>. Particularly worrying was the presence of Cuban construction workers and military personnel who were building a 10,000-foot (3,000&#160;m) airstrip on Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-Gailey_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gailey-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bishop had stated the purpose of the airstrip was to allow commercial jets to land, but US military analysts argued that the only reason for constructing such a long and reinforced runway was so that it could be used by heavy military transport planes. The contractors, American and European companies, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a>, which provided partial funding, all claimed the airstrip did not have military capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Gailey_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gailey-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Reagan was worried that Cuba&#160;&#8211;&#32;under the direction of the Soviet Union&#160;&#8211;&#32;would use Grenada as a refuelling stop for Cuban and Soviet aeroplanes loaded with weapons destined for Central American communist insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 25, 1983, combined forces from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and from the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Security_System" title="Regional Security System">Regional Security System</a> (RSS) based in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> invaded Grenada in an operation codenamed <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">Operation Urgent Fury</a></i>. The US stated this was done at the behest of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Eugenia_Charles" title="Eugenia Charles">Eugenia Charles</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>. While the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">Governor-General</a> of Grenada, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scoon" title="Paul Scoon">Sir Paul Scoon</a>, later stated that he had also requested the invasion,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> it was highly criticised by the governments of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> condemned it as "a flagrant violation of international law" by a vote of 108 in favour to 9, with 27 abstentions.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Resolution_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Resolution-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_Resolution_Vote_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Resolution_Vote-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> considered a similar resolution, which was supported by 11 nations and opposed by only one \xe2\x80\x94 the United States, which vetoed the motion.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-invasion_arrests">Post-invasion arrests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Post-invasion arrests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the invasion of the island nation, the pre-revolutionary Grenadian constitution came into operation once again. Eighteen members of the PRG and the PRA (army) were arrested after the invasion on charges related to the murder of Maurice Bishop and seven others. The eighteen included the top political leadership of Grenada at the time of the execution as well as the entire military chain of command directly responsible for the operation that led to the executions. Fourteen were <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">sentenced to death</a>, one was found not guilty and three were sentenced to 45 years in prison. The death sentences were eventually commuted to terms of imprisonment. Those in prison have become known as the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_17" title="Grenada 17">Grenada 17</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grenada_since_1983">Grenada since 1983</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grenada since 1983">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When US troops withdrew from Grenada in December 1983, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Brathwaite" title="Nicholas Brathwaite">Nicholas Brathwaite</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Grenada)" title="National Democratic Congress (Grenada)">National Democratic Congress</a> was appointed prime minister of an interim administration by Scoon until elections could be organised. The first democratic elections since 1976 were held in December 1984, and were won by the <a href="/wiki/Grenada_National_Party" title="Grenada National Party">Grenada National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Blaize" title="Herbert Blaize">Herbert Blaize</a> who served as prime minister until his death in December 1989.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ben_Jones_(Grenada)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ben Jones (Grenada)">Ben Jones</a> succeeded Blaize as prime minister and served until the March 1990 election, which was won by the National Democratic Congress under Nicholas Brathwaite who returned as prime minister for a second time until he resigned in February 1995. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/George_Brizan" title="George Brizan">George Brizan</a> who served until the June 1995 election which was won by the <a href="/wiki/New_National_Party_(Grenada)" title="New National Party (Grenada)">New National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Keith_Mitchell" title="Keith Mitchell">Keith Mitchell</a> who went on to win the 1999 and 2003 elections and served for a record 13 years until 2008.\n</p><p>In 2000\xe2\x80\x9302, much of the controversy of the late 1970s and early 1980s was once again brought into the public consciousness with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Truth_and_reconciliation_commission" title="Truth and reconciliation commission">truth and reconciliation commission</a>. The commission was chaired by a <a href="/wiki/Holy_Orders" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Orders">Roman Catholic priest</a>, Father Mark Haynes, and was tasked with uncovering injustices arising from the PRA, Bishop\'s regime, and before. It held a number of hearings around the country. Brother Robert Fanovich, head of Presentation Brothers\' College (PBC) in St. George\'s tasked some of his senior students with conducting a research project into the era and specifically into the fact that Maurice Bishop\'s body was never discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Paterson also uncovered that there was still a lot of resentment in Grenadian society resulting from the era and a feeling that there were many injustices still unaddressed.\n</p><p>On September 7, 2004, after being hurricane-free for 49 years, the island was directly hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a>. Ivan struck as a <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 3 hurricane</a> and damaged or destroyed 90% of the island\'s homes. On July 14, 2005, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Emily_(2005)" title="Hurricane Emily (2005)">Hurricane Emily</a>, a Category 1 hurricane at the time, struck the northern part of the island with 80-knot (150&#160;km/h; 92&#160;mph) winds, causing an estimated <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">USD</a> $110&#160;million (EC$297&#160;million) worth of damage. By December 2005, 96% of all hotel rooms were open for business and to have been upgraded in facilities and strengthened to an improved <a href="/wiki/Building_code" title="Building code">building code</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural industry</a> and in particular the <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> industry suffered serious losses, but that event has begun changes in crop management and it is hoped that as new nutmeg trees gradually mature, the industry will return to its pre-Ivan position as a major supplier in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In April 2007, Grenada jointly hosted (along with several other Caribbean nations) the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a>. The Island\'s Prime Minister was the <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a> representative on cricket and was instrumental in having the World Cup games brought to the region. After Hurricane Ivan, the government of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a> (PRC) paid for the new $40&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Park, Grenada">national stadium</a> and provided the aid of over 300 labourers to build and repair it.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> During the opening ceremony, the anthem of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (ROC, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>) was accidentally played instead of the PRC\'s anthem, leading to the firing of top officials.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2008 election was won by the National Democratic Congress under <a href="/wiki/Tillman_Thomas" title="Tillman Thomas">Tillman Thomas</a>. \n</p><p>The 2013 election was won by the <a href="/wiki/New_National_Party_(Grenada)" title="New National Party (Grenada)">New National Party</a> under <a href="/wiki/Keith_Mitchell" title="Keith Mitchell">Keith Mitchell</a> winning all 15 seats.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Grenada" title="Geography of Grenada">Geography of Grenada</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/310px-Grenada-map.png" width="310" height="384" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/465px-Grenada-map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Grenada-map.png/620px-Grenada-map.png 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="1191" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Grenada</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/400px-Grenada2010.jpg" width="400" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/600px-Grenada2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Grenada2010.jpg/800px-Grenada2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aerial photo of the capital <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George&#39;s, Grenada">St George\'s</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The island of Carriacou is the largest island in <a href="/wiki/The_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="The Grenadines">the Grenadines</a>. It is located between the Caribbean Sea and Atlantic Ocean, north of Trinidad and Tobago. Smaller islands are <a href="/wiki/Petite_Martinique" title="Petite Martinique">Petite Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronde_Island" title="Ronde Island">Ronde Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caille_Island" title="Caille Island">Caille Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Island_(Grenadines)" title="Diamond Island (Grenadines)">Diamond Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Large_Island" title="Large Island">Large Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saline_Island" title="Saline Island">Saline Island</a>, and Frigate Island. Most of the population lives on Grenada, and major towns there include the capital, St. George\'s, <a href="/wiki/Grenville,_Grenada" title="Grenville, Grenada">Grenville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gouyave" title="Gouyave">Gouyave</a>. The largest settlement on the other islands is <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Hillsborough, Grenada">Hillsborough</a> on Carriacou.\n</p><p>The islands are of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> origin with extremely rich soil. Grenada\'s interior is very mountainous with <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Catherine_(Grenada)" title="Mount Saint Catherine (Grenada)">Mount St. Catherine</a> being the highest at 840&#160;m (2,760&#160;ft). Several small <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">rivers</a> with beautiful waterfalls flow into the sea from these mountains.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> is tropical: hot and humid in the <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">rainy season</a> and cooled by the <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade wind">trade winds</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>. Grenada, being on the southern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane belt">hurricane belt</a>, has suffered only three hurricanes in fifty years.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Janet" title="Hurricane Janet">Hurricane Janet</a> passed over Grenada on September 23, 1955, with winds of 185&#160;km/h (115&#160;mph), causing severe damage. The most recent storms to hit have been Hurricane Ivan on September 7, 2004, causing severe damage and thirty-nine deaths and Hurricane Emily on July 14, 2005, causing serious damage in Carriacou and in the north of Grenada which had been relatively lightly affected by Hurricane Ivan.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Grenada" title="Politics of Grenada">Politics of Grenada</a></div>\n<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> is <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Grenada" title="Monarchy of Grenada">Queen of Grenada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of State">Head of State</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">The Crown</a> is represented by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors-General of Grenada">Governor-General</a>, currently C\xc3\xa9cile La Grenade. Day-to-day <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> lies with the Head of Government, the Prime Minister. Although appointed by the Governor-General, the Prime Minister is usually the leader of the largest party in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Grenada" title="Parliament of Grenada">Parliament</a>.\n</p><p>The Parliament consists of a Senate (thirteen members) and a House of Representatives (fifteen members). The senators are appointed by the government and the opposition, while the representatives are elected by the population for five-year terms.\n</p><p>On February 19, 2013, Prime Minister Keith Claudius Mitchell, 65, led the New National Party (NNP) to victory with a clean sweep of 15 seats. Mitchell is Grenada\'s ninth prime minister since it attained political independence from Britain in 1974.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_parties">Political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Congress_(Grenada)" title="National Democratic Congress (Grenada)">National Democratic Congress (Grenada)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_National_Party_(Grenada)" title="New National Party (Grenada)">New National Party</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Grenada_United_Labour_Party" title="Grenada United Labour Party">Grenada United Labour Party</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Grenada" title="Foreign relations of Grenada">Foreign relations of Grenada</a></div>\n<p>Grenada is a full and participating member of both the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community (CARICOM)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Commonwealth">The Commonwealth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Commonwealth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Grenada is, along with much of the Caribbean region, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. the organisation, which is primarily the old British colonies, focuses on fostering international relations between its members.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Organisation_of_American_States_.28OAS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_of_American_States_(OAS)">Organisation of American States (OAS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Organisation of American States (OAS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Grenada is one of the thirty five (35) states which has ratified the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">OAS</a> charter and is a member of the Organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The Charter of the Organisation of American States was signed in Bogota in 1948 and was amended by several protocols which were agreed to in different countries. The naming convention which is used with respect to the naming of the protocols is name of the city and the year in which the Protocol was signed, being included in the Protocol, such as Cartagena de Indias in 1985, Managua 1993, according to the website of the OAS.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Grenada entered into the Inter-American system in 1975 according to the OAS\'s website.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits_of_the_Americas">Summits of the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Summits of the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The last <a href="/wiki/Summits_of_the_Americas" title="Summits of the Americas">Summit of the Americas</a>, the seventh, was held in Panama City, Panama in 2015 with the eight summit being held in Lima, Peru in 2018 according to the website of the Summits of Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Since Grenada is a member of the OAS, in light of changes in the global economy, discoveries in the Oil and Gas sector in Guyana, possible exploration for Oil and Gas which is in the discussion stage in Grenada, representations on behalf of Grenada are likely to be made at that Summit.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty">Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On July 6, 1994 at <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Erskine_Sandiford_Centre" title="Lloyd Erskine Sandiford Centre">Sherbourne Conference Centre</a>, St. Michael, Barbados, George Brizan signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty on behalf of the Government of Grenada.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Seven other countries signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty on that day. These countries were: Antigua &amp; Barbuda, Belize, Jamaica, St. Kitts &amp; Nevis, St. Lucia, St. Vincent &amp; The Grenadines, Trinidad and Tobago, with another country Guyana signing the agreement on August 18, 1994. This treaty covered concepts such as taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On June 30, 2014, Grenada signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America in relation to Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act (FATCA).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Grenada\'s military has two branches:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Grenada" title="Law enforcement in Grenada">Royal Grenada Police Force</a>, which includes a Special Service Unit.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coast_Guard_of_Grenada" title="Coast Guard of Grenada">Coast Guard of Grenada</a>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Grenada" title="Parishes of Grenada">Parishes of Grenada</a></div>\n<p>Grenada is divided into <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Grenada" title="Parishes of Grenada">six parishes</a>:\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div Martinique">Carriacou and Petite Martinique</a>, two of the Grenadines, have the status of dependency.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Grenada" title="Economy of Grenada">Economy of Grenada</a></div><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Tone" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section\'s <b>tone or style may not reflect the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">encyclopedic tone</a> used on Wikipedia</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> See Wikipedia\'s <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">guide to writing better articles</a> for suggestions.</span>  <small><i>(May 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/220px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/330px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg/440px-Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Myris_fragr_Fr_080112-3294_ltn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">Nutmeg</a> fruit in <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Grenada\'s economic picture is soured by a heavy external debt problem.  With government debt service payments running at about 25% of total revenues in 2017, Grenada was listed 9th worst in a study of 126 developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Tourist facilities are being expanded; <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> is the leading <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> earner. Major short-term concerns are the rising <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Government budget deficit">fiscal deficit</a> and the deterioration in the external account balance. Grenada shares a common <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> and a common <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> (the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="East Caribbean dollar">East Caribbean dollar</a>) with seven other members of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_exports">Agriculture and exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Agriculture and exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Grenada is a leading producer of several different spices. <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">Cinnamon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloves" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloves">cloves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a>, allspice, orange/citrus peels, wild coffee used by the locals, and especially <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>, providing 20% of the world supply, are all important exports. Grenada is the world\'s second largest producer of nutmeg (after Indonesia), with nutmeg depicted on the Grenadian flag.\n</p><p>The Grenada Chocolate Company has pioneered the cultivation of organic cocoa, which is also processed into finished bars.\n</p><p>In 2017, the Pure Chocolate Festival will be celebrating its fourth year of existence as a formal festival.<sup id="cite_ref-grenadachocolatefest.com_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenadachocolatefest.com-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Some of the activities which have taken place according to the website Grenada Chocolate Festival are visits to the cocoa farms which have been in existence for approximately one hundred (100) years and which are located in rainforests which are ecologically sensitive; dance the cocoa which is a traditional way to separate the skins from the seed of the cocoa or sample cocoa infused cuisine which may have been developed as part of the culture of the country.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada_banner.jpg" class="image" title="Skyline of St. George&#39;s"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Grenada_banner.jpg/1000px-Grenada_banner.jpg" width="1000" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Grenada_banner.jpg/1500px-Grenada_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Grenada_banner.jpg/2000px-Grenada_banner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="300" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grenada_banner.jpg" title="File:Grenada banner.jpg"> </a></div>Skyline of <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Grenada" title="St. George&#39;s, Grenada">St. George\'s</a></div>\n</div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">Tourism</a> is Grenada\'s main economic force. Conventional beach and water-sports tourism is largely focused in the southwest region around St George, the airport and the coastal strip. <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</a> is growing in significance. Most small ecofriendly guesthouses are located in the <a href="/wiki/Saint_David_Parish,_Grenada" title="Saint David Parish, Grenada">Saint David</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_Parish,_Grenada" title="Saint John Parish, Grenada">Saint John</a> parishes. The tourism industry is increasing dramatically with the construction of a large cruise ship pier and esplanade. Up to four cruise ships per day were visiting St. Georges in 2007\xe2\x80\x932008 during the cruise ship season.\n</p><p>Tourism is concentrated in the southwest of the island, around St. George, Grand Anse, Lance Aux Epines, and Point Salines. Grenada has many idyllic beaches around its coastline including the 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) long Grand Anse Beach in St George which is considered to be one of the finest beaches in the world and often appears in countdowns of the world\'s top ten beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Besides these excellent beaches, tourists\' favourite points of interest yet in Grenada are the waterfalls. The nearest to St. George\'s is the Annandale Waterfalls, but other notable ones like Mt. Carmel, Concord, Seven Sisters and Tufton Hall are also within easy reach.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_and_historical_places">Natural and historical places</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Natural and historical places">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/220px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/330px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg/440px-Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Anse_Beach_Grenada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Grand Anse Beach, St. George</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2017 the Carriacou Maroon &amp; String Band Music Festival enters its seventh year.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, occurring in April, the event lasts for three days, occurs in three venues, however it is classified as one festival according to the pure Grenada website.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The concept of String Bands is historical in nature.\n</p><p>In 2017 the Annual Budget Marine Spice Island BillFish Tournament (48) will be entering its 48th year of existence. The Tournament lasts for four days and in 2017 it starts on Jan 21.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Island Water World Sailing Week, as its name suggests,<sup id="cite_ref-grenadasailingweek.com_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grenadasailingweek.com-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> is an event which lasts for a week and in 2017 will be held towards the end of January into February. This event is similar to the America Cup which is hosted upon agreement or calling out.\n</p><p>Many of these events stimulate the economy as they attract boats and persons who may need repairs to their boats or who may need to learn new routes to shelter their boats during hurricanes or Inter Tropical Convergence Zones (ITCZs) which are weather systems which affect this part of the world for almost half of the year every year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Grenada Sailing Festival Work Boat Regatta starts in January and lasts for a few days. From the photos on the website Grenada Sailing Festival, it appears that the style of the race is similar is similar to that event in which CARICOM national, Andrew Lewis raced at the 2016 Summer Olympics.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_University" title="St. George&#39;s University">St. George\'s University</a> has rapidly expanded in recent years, and has a major economic impact, particularly in southern portions of the island. While some of its approximately 5,000 students are from Grenada, including many undergraduates, and many medical students serve rotations off of the island, the majority of students are from other countries and bring substantial revenue to the island while studying there. St. George\'s University is among the island\'s largest employers, and students patronise many off-campus landlords and other businesses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>St. George\'s University is one of the Organisation of American States (OAS) Consortium of Universities according to the OAS webpage.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Flights at the <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bishop_International_Airport" title="Maurice Bishop International Airport">Maurice Bishop International Airport</a> connect with other Caribbean islands, the United States, Canada, and Europe. There is a daily fast ferry service between St. George and Hillsborough.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Grenada&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Grenada" title="Demographics of Grenada">Demographics of Grenada</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Afro-Grenadians" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Grenadians">Afro-Grenadians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indo-Grenadians" title="Indo-Grenadians">Indo-Grenadians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carriacou_Scene.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/220px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/330px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Carriacou_Scene.jpg/440px-Carriacou_Scene.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carriacou_Scene.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">Carriacou</a>, with other Grenadine islands visible in the distance</div></div></div>\n<p>A majority of Grenadine citizens (82%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>) are descendants of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> brought by the English and French; few of the indigenous Carib and Arawak population survived the French purge at <a href="/wiki/Sauteurs" title="Sauteurs">Sauteurs</a>. A small percentage of descendants of indentured workers from India were brought to Grenada mainly from the North Indian states of Bihar and Uttar Pradesh between May 1, 1857 \xe2\x80\x93 January 10, 1885. Today, Grenadians of Indian descent comprise the second largest ethnic group. There is also a small community of French and English descendants. The rest of the population is of mixed descent (13%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>).\n</p><p>Grenada, like many of the Caribbean islands is subject to a large amount of migration, with a large number of young people wanting to leave the island to seek life elsewhere. With estimated 107,317&#160;people living in Grenada, estimates and census data suggest that there are at least that number of Grenadian-born people in other parts of the Caribbean (such as Barbados and Trinidad) and at least that number again in <a href="/wiki/First_World" title="First World">First World</a> countries. Popular migration points for Grenadians further north include <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (in particular, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>; see <a href="/wiki/Grenadian_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Grenadian British">Grenadians in the UK</a>) and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, or as far south as <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. This means that probably around a third of those born in Grenada still live there.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
